[1mNAME[0m[m
       logger - a shell command interface to the syslog(3) system log module[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mlogger[0m [options] [message][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mlogger[0m  makes  entries  in the system log.  It provides a shell command[m
       interface to the [1msyslog[0m(3) system log module.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-n[0m, [1m--server[0m [4mserver[24m[m
              Write to the specified remote syslog [4mserver[24m instead  of  to  the[m
              builtin syslog routines.  Unless [1m--udp[0m or [1m--tcp[0m is specified the[m
              logger will first try to use UDP, but if it fails a TCP  connecâ€[m
              tion is attempted.[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--udp[0m[m
              Use  datagram (UDP) only.  By default the connection is tried to[m
              [4msyslog[24m port defined in /etc/services, which is often [4m514[24m.[m
[m

LOGGER(1)                        User Commands                       LOGGER(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       logger - a shell command interface to the syslog(3) system log module[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mlogger[0m [options] [message][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mlogger[0m  makes  entries  in the system log.  It provides a shell command[m
       interface to the [1msyslog[0m(3) system log module.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-n[0m, [1m--server[0m [4mserver[24m[m
              Write to the specified remote syslog [4mserver[24m instead  of  to  the[m
              builtin syslog routines.  Unless [1m--udp[0m or [1m--tcp[0m is specified the[m
              logger will first try to use UDP, but if it fails a TCP  connecâ€[m
              tion is attempted.[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--udp[0m[m
              Use  datagram (UDP) only.  By default the connection is tried to[m
              [4msyslog[24m port defined in /etc/services, which is often [4m514[24m.[m
[m
       [1m-T[0m, [1m--tcp[0m[m
              Use stream (TCP) only.  By default the connection  is  tried  to[m
              [4msyslog-conn[24m port defined in /etc/services, which is often [4m601[24m.[m
[m
       [1m-P[0m, [1m--port[0m [4mport[24m[m
              Use  the specified [4mport[24m.  When this option is not specified, the[m
              port defaults to syslog for udp and to syslog-conn for tcp  conâ€[m
              nections.[m
[m
       [1m-i[0m, [1m--id[0m[m
              Log the process ID of the logger process with each line.[m
[m
       [1m-f[0m, [1m--file[0m [4mfile[24m[m
              Log  the  contents of the specified [4mfile[24m.  This option cannot be[m
              combined with a command-line message.[m
[m
       [1m-h[0m, [1m--help[0m[m
              Display a help text and exit.[m
[m
       [1m-p[0m, [1m--priority[0m [4mpriority[24m[m
              Enter the message into the log with the specified [4mpriority[24m.  The[m
              priority  may  be  specified  numerically or as a [4mfacility.level[24m[m
              pair.  For example, [1m-p[0m [4mlocal3.info[24m logs the message as  informaâ€[m
              tional in the local3 facility.  The default is [4muser.notice[24m.[m

[25;1H              Use stream (TCP) only.  By default the connection  is  tried  to[m
[26;1H              [4msyslog-conn[24m port defined in /etc/services, which is often [4m601[24m.[m
[27;1H[m
[28;1H       [1m-P[0m, [1m--port[0m [4mport[24m[m
[29;1H              Use  the specified [4mport[24m.  When this option is not specified, the[m
[30;1H              port defaults to syslog for udp and to syslog-conn for tcp  conâ€[m
[31;1H              nections.[m
[32;1H[m
[33;1H       [1m-i[0m, [1m--id[0m[m
[34;1H              Log the process ID of the logger process with each line.[m
[35;1H[m
[36;1H       [1m-f[0m, [1m--file[0m [4mfile[24m[m
[37;1H              Log  the  contents of the specified [4mfile[24m.  This option cannot be[m
[38;1H              combined with a command-line message.[m
[39;1H[m
[40;1H       [1m-h[0m, [1m--help[0m[m
[41;1H              Display a help text and exit.[m
[42;1H[m
[43;1H       [1m-p[0m, [1m--priority[0m [4mpriority[24m[m
[44;1H              Enter the message into the log with the specified [4mpriority[24m.  The[m
[45;1H              priority  may  be  specified  numerically or as a [4mfacility.level[24m[m
[46;1H              pair.  For example, [1m-p[0m [4mlocal3.info[24m logs the message as  informaâ€[m
[47;1H              tional in the local3 facility.  The default is [4muser.notice[24m.[m
[48;1H[m
[49;1H[K[7mPattern not found  (press RETURN)[27m[49;1H[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1m-S[0m, [1m--size[0m [4msize[24m[m
              Sets  the  maximum  permitted message size. The default is 1KiB,[m
              which is the limit traditionally used and specified in RFC 3164.[m
              When selecting a maximum message size, it is important to ensure[m
              that the receiver supports the max size as well, otherwise  mesâ€[m
              sages may become truncated.[m
[m
       [1m-s[0m, [1m--stderr[0m[m
              Output  the  message  to standard error as well as to the system[m
              log.[m
[m
       [1m-t[0m, [1m--tag[0m [4mtag[24m[m
              Mark every line to be logged with the specified [4mtag[24m.[m
[m
       [1m-u[0m, [1m--socket[0m [4msocket[24m[m
              Write to the specified [4msocket[24m instead of to the  builtin  syslog[m
              routines.[m
[m
       [1m-V[0m, [1m--version[0m[m
              Display version information and exit.[m
[m
       [1m--[0m     End  the  argument  list.  This is to allow the [4mmessage[24m to start[m
              with a hyphen (-).[m
[m
       [4mmessage[24m[m
              Write the message to log; if not specified, and the [4m-f[24m  flag  is[m
              not provided, standard input is logged.[m
[m
       The [1mlogger[0m utility exits 0 on success, and >0 if an error occurs.[m
[m
[1mFACILITIES[0m [1mAND[0m [1mLEVELS[0m[m
       Valid facility names are:[m
[m
              [1mauth[0m[m
              [1mauthpriv[0m   for security information of a sensitive nature[m
              [1mcron[0m[m
              [1mdaemon[0m[m
              [1mftp[0m[m
              [1mkern[0m       cannot be generated from userspace process, automatically converted to [1muser[0m[m
              [1mlpr[0m[m
              [1mmail[0m[m
              [1mnews[0m[m
              [1msyslog[0m[m
              [1muser[0m[m
              [1muucp[0m[m
              [1mlocal0[0m[m
                to[m
              [1mlocal7[0m[m
[7m Manual page logger(1) line 51/137 76% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              [1msecurity[0m   deprecated synonym for [1mauth[0m[m
[m
       Valid level names are:[m
[m
              [1memerg[0m[m
              [1malert[0m[m
              [1mcrit[0m[m
              [1merr[0m[m
              [1mwarning[0m[m
              [1mnotice[0m[m
              [1minfo[0m[m
              [1mdebug[0m[m
              [1mpanic[0m     deprecated synonym for [1memerg[0m[m
              [1merror[0m     deprecated synonym for [1merr[0m[m
              [1mwarn[0m      deprecated synonym for [1mwarning[0m[m
[m
       For  the  priority  order and intended purposes of these facilities and[m
       levels, see [1msyslog[0m(3).[m
[m
[1mEXAMPLES[0m[m
       logger System rebooted[m
       logger -p local0.notice -t HOSTIDM -f /dev/idmc[m
       logger -n loghost.example.com System rebooted[m
[m

       [1msyslog[0m(3), [1msyslogd[0m(8)[m

       patible.[m

[?1049h[?1h=LOGGER(1)                                                                                 User Commands                                                                                 LOGGER(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       logger - a shell command interface to the syslog(3) system log module[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mlogger[0m [options] [message][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mlogger[0m makes entries in the system log.  It provides a shell command interface to the [1msyslog[0m(3) system log module.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-n[0m, [1m--server[0m [4mserver[24m[m
              Write  to the specified remote syslog [4mserver[24m instead of to the builtin syslog routines.  Unless [1m--udp[0m or [1m--tcp[0m is specified the logger will first try to use UDP, but if it fails a[m
              TCP connection is attempted.[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--udp[0m[m
              Use datagram (UDP) only.  By default the connection is tried to [4msyslog[24m port defined in /etc/services, which is often [4m514[24m.[m
[m
       [1m-T[0m, [1m--tcp[0m[m
              Use stream (TCP) only.  By default the connection is tried to [4msyslog-conn[24m port defined in /etc/services, which is often [4m601[24m.[m
[m
       [1m-P[0m, [1m--port[0m [4mport[24m[m
              Use the specified [4mport[24m.  When this option is not specified, the port defaults to syslog for udp and to syslog-conn for tcp connections.[m
[m
       [1m-i[0m, [1m--id[0m[m
              Log the process ID of the logger process with each line.[m
[m
       [1m-f[0m, [1m--file[0m [4mfile[24m[m
              Log the contents of the specified [4mfile[24m.  This option cannot be combined with a command-line message.[m
[m
       [1m-h[0m, [1m--help[0m[m
              Display a help text and exit.[m
[m
       [1m-p[0m, [1m--priority[0m [4mpriority[24m[m
              Enter the message into the log with the specified [4mpriority[24m.  The priority may be specified numerically or as a [4mfacility.level[24m pair.  For example, [1m-p[0m [4mlocal3.info[24m logs  the  message[m
              as informational in the local3 facility.  The default is [4muser.notice[24m.[m
[m
       [1m-S[0m, [1m--size[0m [4msize[24m[m
              Sets  the maximum permitted message size. The default is 1KiB, which is the limit traditionally used and specified in RFC 3164. When selecting a maximum message size, it is imporâ€[m
              tant to ensure that the receiver supports the max size as well, otherwise messages may become truncated.[m
[m
       [1m-s[0m, [1m--stderr[0m[m
              Output the message to standard error as well as to the system log.[m
[m
       [1m-t[0m, [1m--tag[0m [4mtag[24m[m
              Mark every line to be logged with the specified [4mtag[24m.[m
[m

    inet 10.252.0.1/16 brd 10.252.255.255 scope global eth1

    inet6 fe80::5054:ff:fe00:0/64 scope link

[?1049h[?1h=IP(8)                                                                                         Linux                                                                                         IP(8)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       ip - show / manipulate routing, devices, policy routing and tunnels[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mip[0m [ [4mOPTIONS[24m ] [4mOBJECT[24m { [4mCOMMAND[24m | [1mhelp[0m }[m
[m
       [1mip[0m [ [1m-force[0m ] [1m-batch[0m [4mfilename[24m[m
[m
       [4mOBJECT[24m := { [1mlink[0m | [1maddress[0m | [1maddrlabel[0m | [1mroute[0m | [1mrule[0m | [1mneigh[0m | [1mntable[0m | [1mtunnel[0m | [1mtuntap[0m | [1mmaddress[0m | [1mmroute[0m | [1mmrule[0m | [1mmonitor[0m | [1mxfrm[0m | [1mnetns[0m | [1ml2tp[0m | [1mtcp_metrics[0m | [1mtoken[0m }[m
[m
       [4mOPTIONS[24m := { [1m-V[0m[[4mersion[24m] | [1m-h[0m[[4muman-readable[24m] | [1m-s[0m[[4mtatistics[24m] | [1m-d[0m[[4metails[24m] | [1m-r[0m[[4mesolve[24m] | [1m-iec[0m | [1m-f[0m[[4mamily[24m] { [1minet[0m | [1minet6[0m | [1mipx[0m | [1mdnet[0m | [1mlink[0m } | [1m-4[0m | [1m-6[0m | [1m-I[0m | [1m-D[0m | [1m-B[0m | [1m-0[0m | [1m-l[0m[[4moops[24m] {[m
               [1mmaximum-addr-flush-attempts[0m } | [1m-o[0m[[4mneline[24m] | [1m-rc[0m[[4mvbuf[24m] [[1msize[0m] | [1m-t[0m[[4mimestamp[24m] | [1m-ts[0m[[4mhort[24m] | [1m-n[0m[[4metns[24m] name | [1m-a[0m[[4mll[24m] }[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-V[0m, [1m-Version[0m[m
              Print the version of the [1mip[0m utility and exit.[m
[m
       [1m-h[0m, [1m-human[0m, [1m-human-readable[0m[m
              output statistics with human readable values followed by suffix.[m
[m
       [1m-b[0m, [1m-batch[0m <FILENAME>[m
[7m Manual page ip(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              Read commands from provided file or standard input and invoke them.  First failure will cause termination of ip.[m
[m
       [1m-force[0m Don't terminate ip on errors in batch mode.  If there were any errors during execution of the commands, the application return code will be non zero.[m
[m
       [1m-s[0m, [1m-stats[0m, [1m-statistics[0m[m
              Output more information. If the option appears twice or more, the amount of information increases.  As a rule, the information is statistics or some time values.[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m-details[0m[m
              Output more detailed information.[m
[m
       [1m-l[0m, [1m-loops[0m <COUNT>[m
              Specify maximum number of loops the 'ip address flush' logic will attempt before giving up. The default is 10.  Zero (0) means loop until all addresses are removed.[m
[m
       [1m-f[0m, [1m-family[0m <FAMILY>[m
              Specifies the protocol family to use. The protocol family identifier can be one of [1minet[0m, [1minet6[0m, [1mbridge[0m, [1mipx[0m, [1mdnet[0m or [1mlink[0m.  If this option is not present, the protocol family is[m
              guessed from other arguments. If the rest of the command line does not give enough information to guess the family, [1mip[0m falls back to the default one, usually [1minet[0m or [1many[0m.  [1mlink[0m is[m
              a special family identifier meaning that no networking protocol is involved.[m
[m
       [1m-4[0m     shortcut for [1m-family[0m [1minet[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-6[0m     shortcut for [1m-family[0m [1minet6[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-B[0m     shortcut for [1m-family[0m [1mbridge[0m.[m
[7m Manual page ip(8) line 33 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       [1m-D[0m     shortcut for [1m-family[0m [1mdecnet[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-I[0m     shortcut for [1m-family[0m [1mipx[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-0[0m     shortcut for [1m-family[0m [1mlink[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-o[0m, [1m-oneline[0m[m
              output each record on a single line, replacing line feeds with the [1m'\'[0m character. This is convenient when you want to count records with [1mwc[0m(1) or to [1mgrep[0m(1) the output.[m
[m
       [1m-r[0m, [1m-resolve[0m[m
              use the system's name resolver to print DNS names instead of host addresses.[m
[m
       [1m-n[0m, [1m-netns[0m <NETNS>[m
              switches [1mip[0m to the specified network namespace [4mNETNS[24m.  Actually it just simplifies executing of:[m
[m
              [1mip[0m [1mnetns[0m [1mexec[0m [4mNETNS[24m [1mip[0m [ [4mOPTIONS[24m ] [4mOBJECT[24m { [4mCOMMAND[24m | [1mhelp[0m }[m
[m
              to[m
[m
              [1mip[0m -n[etns] [4mNETNS[24m [ [4mOPTIONS[24m ] [4mOBJECT[24m { [4mCOMMAND[24m | [1mhelp[0m }[m
[m
       [1m-a[0m, [1m-all[0m[m
[7m Manual page ip(8) line 64 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              executes specified command over all objects, it depends if command supports this option.[m
[m
       [1m-t[0m, [1m-timestamp[0m[m
              display current time when using monitor option.[m
[m
       [1m-ts[0m, [1m-tshort[0m[m
              Like [1m-timestamp[0m, but use shorter format.[m
[m
       [1m-rc[0m, [1m-rcvbuf[0m<SIZE>[m
              Set the netlink socket receive buffer size, defaults to 1MB.[m
[m
       [1m-iec[0m   print human readable rates in IEC units (e.g. 1Ki = 1024).[m
[m
       [1m-t[0m, [1m-timestamp[0m[m
              display current time when using monitor option.[m
[m
[1mIP[0m [1m-[0m [1mCOMMAND[0m [1mSYNTAX[0m[m
   [4mOBJECT[24m[m
       [1maddress[0m[m
              - protocol (IP or IPv6) address on a device.[m
[m
       [1maddrlabel[0m[m
              - label configuration for protocol address selection.[m
[7m Manual page ip(8) line 94 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       [1ml2tp[0m   - tunnel ethernet over IP (L2TPv3).[m
[m
       [1mlink[0m   - network device.[m
[m
       [1mmaddress[0m[m
              - multicast address.[m
[m
       [1mmonitor[0m[m
              - watch for netlink messages.[m
[m
       [1mmroute[0m - multicast routing cache entry.[m
[m
       [1mmrule[0m  - rule in multicast routing policy database.[m
[m
       [1mneighbour[0m[m
              - manage ARP or NDISC cache entries.[m
[m
       [1mnetns[0m  - manage network namespaces.[m
[m
       [1mntable[0m - manage the neighbor cache's operation.[m
[m
       [1mroute[0m  - routing table entry.[m
[7m Manual page ip(8) line 124 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       [1mrule[0m   - rule in routing policy database.[m
[m
       [1mtcp_metrics/tcpmetrics[0m[m
              - manage TCP Metrics[m
[m
       [1mtoken[0m  - manage tokenized interface identifiers.[m
[m
       [1mtunnel[0m - tunnel over IP.[m
[m
       [1mtuntap[0m - manage TUN/TAP devices.[m
[m
       [1mxfrm[0m   - manage IPSec policies.[m
[m
       The names of all objects may be written in full or abbreviated form, for exampe [1maddress[0m can be abbreviated as [1maddr[0m or just [1ma.[0m[m
[m
   [4mCOMMAND[24m[m
       Specifies the action to perform on the object.  The set of possible actions depends on the object type.  As a rule, it is possible to [1madd[0m, [1mdelete[0m and [1mshow[0m (or [1mlist[0m ) objects, but some[m
       objects do not allow all of these operations or have some additional commands. The [1mhelp[0m command is available for all objects. It prints out a list of available commands and argument synâ€[m
       tax conventions.[m
[m
       If no command is given, some default command is assumed.  Usually it is [1mlist[0m or, if the objects of this class cannot be listed, [1mhelp[0m.[m

[HM[m

[HM[m

#### MODULES ####

# The imjournal module bellow is now used as a message source instead of imuxsock.
$ModLoad imuxsock # provides support for local system logging (e.g. via logger command)
$ModLoad imjournal # provides access to the systemd journal
#$ModLoad imklog # reads kernel messages (the same are read from journald)
#$ModLoad immark  # provides --MARK-- message capability

# Provides UDP syslog reception
#$ModLoad imudp
#$UDPServerRun 514

# Provides TCP syslog reception
$ModLoad imtcp
$InputTCPServerRun 514

[?1049h[?1h=LOGROTATE(8)                     System Administrator's Manual                     LOGROTATE(8)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       logrotate â€ rotates, compresses, and mails system logs[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m [[1m-dv[0m] [[1m-f[0m|[1m--force[0m] [[1m-s[0m|[1m--state[0m [4mfile[24m] [4mconfig_file[24m ..[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m  is  designed to ease administration of systems that generate large numbers of[m
       log files.  It allows automatic rotation,  compression,  removal,  and  mailing  of  log[m
       files.  Each log file may be handled daily, weekly, monthly, or when it grows too large.[m
[m
       Normally, [1mlogrotate[0m is run as a daily cron job.  It will not modify a log multiple times[m
       in one day unless the criterion for that log is based on the log's size and [1mlogrotate[0m is[m
       being run multiple times each day, or unless the [1m-f[0m or [1m--force[0m option is used.[m
[m
       Any  number  of  config  files  may be given on the command line. Later config files may[m
       override the options given in earlier files, so the order in which the [1mlogrotate[0m  config[m
       files  are listed is important.  Normally, a single config file which includes any other[m
       config files which are needed should be used.  See below for more information on how  to[m
       use  the  [1minclude[0m  directive to accomplish this.  If a directory is given on the command[m
       line, every file in that directory is used as a config file.[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       If no command line arguments are given,  [1mlogrotate[0m  will  print  version  and  copyright[m
       information, along with a short usage summary.  If any errors occur while rotating logs,[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m will exit with non-zero status.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-?[0m, [1m--help[0m[m
              Prints help message.[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--debug[0m[m
              Turns on debug mode and implies [1m-v[0m.  In debug mode, no changes will  be  made  to[m
              the logs or to the [1mlogrotate[0m state file.[m
[m
       [1m-f[0m, [1m--force[0m[m
              Tells  [1mlogrotate[0m  to  force the rotation, even if it doesn't think this is necesâ€[m
              sary.  Sometimes this is useful after adding new entries to  a  [1mlogrotate[0m  config[m
              file,  or  if  old  log files have been removed by hand, as the new files will be[m
              created, and logging will continue correctly.[m
[m
       [1m-m[0m, [1m--mail[0m [1m<command>[0m[m
              Tells [1mlogrotate[0m which command to use  when  mailing  logs.  This  command  should[m
              accept  two  arguments:  1) the subject of the message, and 2) the recipient. The[m
              command must then read a message on standard input and mail it to the  recipient.[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 26 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              The default mail command is [1m/bin/mail[0m [1m-s[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-s[0m, [1m--state[0m [1m<statefile>[0m[m
              Tells  [1mlogrotate[0m  to use an alternate state file.  This is useful if logrotate is[m
              being run as a different user for various sets of log files.  The  default  state[m
              file is [4m/var/lib/logrotate/logrotate.status[24m.[m
[m
       [1m--usage[0m[m
              Prints a short usage message.[m
[m
       +[1m-v[0m, [1m--verbose[0m[m
              Turns on verbose mode.[m
[m
[1mCONFIGURATION[0m [1mFILE[0m[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m  reads everything about the log files it should be handling from the series of[m
       configuration files specified on the command line.   Each  configuration  file  can  set[m
       global  options  (local definitions override global ones, and later definitions override[m
       earlier ones) and specify logfiles to rotate. A simple  configuration  file  looks  like[m
       this:[m
[m
       # sample logrotate configuration file[m
       compress[m
[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 53 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       /var/log/messages {[m
           rotate 5[m
           weekly[m
           postrotate[m
               /usr/bin/killall -HUP syslogd[m
           endscript[m
       }[m
[m
       "/var/log/httpd/access.log" /var/log/httpd/error.log {[m
           rotate 5[m
           mail www@my.org[m
           size 100k[m
           sharedscripts[m
           postrotate[m
               /usr/bin/killall -HUP httpd[m
           endscript[m
       }[m
[m
       /var/log/news/* {[m
           monthly[m
           rotate 2[m
           olddir /var/log/news/old[m
           missingok[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 80 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K           postrotate[m
               kill -HUP `cat /var/run/inn.pid`[m
           endscript[m
           nocompress[m
       }[m
[m
       ~/log/*.log {}[m
[m
       The  first  few lines set global options; in the example, logs are compressed after they[m
       are rotated.  Note that comments may appear anywhere in the config file as long  as  the[m
       first non-whitespace character on the line is a #.[m
[m
       The  next  section  of the config files defined how to handle the log file [4m/var/log/mesâ€[24m[m
       [4msages[24m. The log will go through five weekly rotations before being removed. After the log[m
       file  has  been rotated (but before the old version of the log has been compressed), the[m
       command [4m/sbin/killall[24m [4m-HUP[24m [4msyslogd[24m will be executed.[m
[m
       The  next  section  defines  the  parameters  for  both  [4m/var/log/httpd/access.log[24m   and[m
       [4m/var/log/httpd/error.log[24m.  They are rotated whenever it grows over 100k in size, and the[m
       old logs files are mailed (uncompressed) to www@my.org after going through 5  rotations,[m
       rather  than being removed. The [1msharedscripts[0m means that the [1mpostrotate[0m script will only[m
       be run once (after the old logs have been compressed), not once for each  log  which  is[m
       rotated.  Note that the double quotes around the first filename at the beginning of this[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 103 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       section allows logrotate to rotate logs with spaces in the name.  Normal  shell  quoting[m
       rules apply, with ', ", and \ characters supported.[m
[m
       The next section defines the parameters for all of the files in [4m/var/log/news[24m. Each file[m
       is rotated on a monthly basis.  This is considered a single rotation  directive  and  if[m
       errors occur for more than one file, the log files are not compressed.[m
[m
       The  last  section uses tilde expansion to rotate log files in the home directory of the[m
       current user. This is only available, if your glob library supports tilde expansion. GNU[m
       glob does support this.[m
[m
       Please  use  wildcards with caution.  If you specify *, [1mlogrotate[0m will rotate all files,[m
       including previously rotated ones.  A way around this is to use the [1molddir[0m directive  or[m
       a more exact wildcard (such as *.log).[m
[m
       Here is more information on the directives which may be included in a [1mlogrotate[0m configuâ€[m
       ration file:[m
[m
       [1mcompress[0m[m
              Old versions of log files are compressed with [1mgzip[0m(1) by default. See also [1mnocomâ€[0m[m
              [1mpress[0m.[m
[m
       [1mcompresscmd[0m[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 128 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              Specifies  which command to use to compress log files.  The default is [1mgzip[0m.  See[m
              also [1mcompress[0m.[m
[m
       [1muncompresscmd[0m[m
              Specifies which command to use to uncompress log files.  The default is [1mgunzip[0m.[m
[m
       [1mcompressext[0m[m
              Specifies which extension to  use  on  compressed  logfiles,  if  compression  is[m
              enabled.  The default follows that of the configured compression command.[m
[m
       [1mcompressoptions[0m[m
              Command  line options may be passed to the compression program, if one is in use.[m
              The default, for [1mgzip[0m(1), is "-6" (biased towards high compression at the expense[m
              of  speed).   If  you use a different compression command, you may need to change[m
              the [1mcompressoptions[0m to match.[m
[m
       [1mcopy[0m   Make a copy of the log file, but don't change the original at all.   This  option[m
              can  be  used,  for instance, to make a snapshot of the current log file, or when[m
              some other utility needs to truncate or parse the  file.   When  this  option  is[m
              used, the [1mcreate[0m option will have no effect, as the old log file stays in place.[m
[m
       [1mcopytruncate[0m[m
              Truncate  the original log file in place after creating a copy, instead of moving[m

[?1049h[?1h=LOGROTATE(8)                     System Administrator's Manual                     LOGROTATE(8)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       logrotate â€ rotates, compresses, and mails system logs[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m [[1m-dv[0m] [[1m-f[0m|[1m--force[0m] [[1m-s[0m|[1m--state[0m [4mfile[24m] [4mconfig_file[24m ..[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m  is  designed to ease administration of systems that generate large numbers of[m
       log files.  It allows automatic rotation,  compression,  removal,  and  mailing  of  log[m
       files.  Each log file may be handled daily, weekly, monthly, or when it grows too large.[m
[m
       Normally, [1mlogrotate[0m is run as a daily cron job.  It will not modify a log multiple times[m
       in one day unless the criterion for that log is based on the log's size and [1mlogrotate[0m is[m
       being run multiple times each day, or unless the [1m-f[0m or [1m--force[0m option is used.[m
[m
       Any  number  of  config  files  may be given on the command line. Later config files may[m
       override the options given in earlier files, so the order in which the [1mlogrotate[0m  config[m
       files  are listed is important.  Normally, a single config file which includes any other[m
       config files which are needed should be used.  See below for more information on how  to[m
       use  the  [1minclude[0m  directive to accomplish this.  If a directory is given on the command[m
       line, every file in that directory is used as a config file.[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       If no command line arguments are given,  [1mlogrotate[0m  will  print  version  and  copyright[m
       information, along with a short usage summary.  If any errors occur while rotating logs,[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m will exit with non-zero status.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-?[0m, [1m--help[0m[m
              Prints help message.[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--debug[0m[m
              Turns on debug mode and implies [1m-v[0m.  In debug mode, no changes will  be  made  to[m
              the logs or to the [1mlogrotate[0m state file.[m
[m
       [1m-f[0m, [1m--force[0m[m
              Tells  [1mlogrotate[0m  to  force the rotation, even if it doesn't think this is necesâ€[m
              sary.  Sometimes this is useful after adding new entries to  a  [1mlogrotate[0m  config[m
              file,  or  if  old  log files have been removed by hand, as the new files will be[m
              created, and logging will continue correctly.[m
[m
       [1m-m[0m, [1m--mail[0m [1m<command>[0m[m
              Tells [1mlogrotate[0m which command to use  when  mailing  logs.  This  command  should[m
              accept  two  arguments:  1) the subject of the message, and 2) the recipient. The[m
              command must then read a message on standard input and mail it to the  recipient.[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 26 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              The default mail command is [1m/bin/mail[0m [1m-s[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-s[0m, [1m--state[0m [1m<statefile>[0m[m
              Tells  [1mlogrotate[0m  to use an alternate state file.  This is useful if logrotate is[m
              being run as a different user for various sets of log files.  The  default  state[m
              file is [4m/var/lib/logrotate/logrotate.status[24m.[m
[m
       [1m--usage[0m[m
              Prints a short usage message.[m
[m
       +[1m-v[0m, [1m--verbose[0m[m
              Turns on verbose mode.[m
[m
[1mCONFIGURATION[0m [1mFILE[0m[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m  reads everything about the log files it should be handling from the series of[m
       configuration files specified on the command line.   Each  configuration  file  can  set[m
       global  options  (local definitions override global ones, and later definitions override[m
       earlier ones) and specify logfiles to rotate. A simple  configuration  file  looks  like[m
       this:[m
[m
       # sample logrotate configuration file[m
       compress[m
[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 53 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       /var/log/messages {[m
           rotate 5[m
           weekly[m
           postrotate[m
               /usr/bin/killall -HUP syslogd[m
           endscript[m
       }[m
[m
       "/var/log/httpd/access.log" /var/log/httpd/error.log {[m
           rotate 5[m
           mail www@my.org[m
           size 100k[m
           sharedscripts[m
           postrotate[m
               /usr/bin/killall -HUP httpd[m
           endscript[m
       }[m
[m
       /var/log/news/* {[m
           monthly[m
           rotate 2[m
           olddir /var/log/news/old[m
           missingok[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 80 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K           postrotate[m
               kill -HUP `cat /var/run/inn.pid`[m
           endscript[m
           nocompress[m
       }[m
[m
       ~/log/*.log {}[m
[m
       The  first  few lines set global options; in the example, logs are compressed after they[m
       are rotated.  Note that comments may appear anywhere in the config file as long  as  the[m
       first non-whitespace character on the line is a #.[m
[m
       The  next  section  of the config files defined how to handle the log file [4m/var/log/mesâ€[24m[m
       [4msages[24m. The log will go through five weekly rotations before being removed. After the log[m
       file  has  been rotated (but before the old version of the log has been compressed), the[m
       command [4m/sbin/killall[24m [4m-HUP[24m [4msyslogd[24m will be executed.[m
[m
       The  next  section  defines  the  parameters  for  both  [4m/var/log/httpd/access.log[24m   and[m
       [4m/var/log/httpd/error.log[24m.  They are rotated whenever it grows over 100k in size, and the[m
       old logs files are mailed (uncompressed) to www@my.org after going through 5  rotations,[m
       rather  than being removed. The [1msharedscripts[0m means that the [1mpostrotate[0m script will only[m
       be run once (after the old logs have been compressed), not once for each  log  which  is[m
       rotated.  Note that the double quotes around the first filename at the beginning of this[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 103 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       section allows logrotate to rotate logs with spaces in the name.  Normal  shell  quoting[m
       rules apply, with ', ", and \ characters supported.[m
[m
       The next section defines the parameters for all of the files in [4m/var/log/news[24m. Each file[m
       is rotated on a monthly basis.  This is considered a single rotation  directive  and  if[m
       errors occur for more than one file, the log files are not compressed.[m
[m
       The  last  section uses tilde expansion to rotate log files in the home directory of the[m
       current user. This is only available, if your glob library supports tilde expansion. GNU[m
       glob does support this.[m
[m
       Please  use  wildcards with caution.  If you specify *, [1mlogrotate[0m will rotate all files,[m
       including previously rotated ones.  A way around this is to use the [1molddir[0m directive  or[m
       a more exact wildcard (such as *.log).[m
[m
       Here is more information on the directives which may be included in a [1mlogrotate[0m configuâ€[m
       ration file:[m
[m
       [1mcompress[0m[m
              Old versions of log files are compressed with [1mgzip[0m(1) by default. See also [1mnocomâ€[0m[m
              [1mpress[0m.[m
[m
       [1mcompresscmd[0m[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 128 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              Specifies  which command to use to compress log files.  The default is [1mgzip[0m.  See[m
              also [1mcompress[0m.[m
[m
       [1muncompresscmd[0m[m
              Specifies which command to use to uncompress log files.  The default is [1mgunzip[0m.[m
[m
       [1mcompressext[0m[m
              Specifies which extension to  use  on  compressed  logfiles,  if  compression  is[m
              enabled.  The default follows that of the configured compression command.[m
[m
       [1mcompressoptions[0m[m
              Command  line options may be passed to the compression program, if one is in use.[m
              The default, for [1mgzip[0m(1), is "-6" (biased towards high compression at the expense[m
              of  speed).   If  you use a different compression command, you may need to change[m
              the [1mcompressoptions[0m to match.[m
[m
       [1mcopy[0m   Make a copy of the log file, but don't change the original at all.   This  option[m
              can  be  used,  for instance, to make a snapshot of the current log file, or when[m
              some other utility needs to truncate or parse the  file.   When  this  option  is[m
              used, the [1mcreate[0m option will have no effect, as the old log file stays in place.[m
[m
       [1mcopytruncate[0m[m
              Truncate  the original log file in place after creating a copy, instead of moving[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 153 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              the old log file and optionally creating a new one.  It can  be  used  when  some[m
              program  cannot  be  told  to  close  its logfile and thus might continue writing[m
              (appending) to the previous log file forever.  Note that there is  a  very  small[m
              time slice between copying the file and truncating it, so some logging data might[m
              be lost.  When this option is used, the [1mcreate[0m option will have no effect, as the[m
              old log file stays in place.[m
[m
       [1mcreate[0m [4mmode[24m [4mowner[24m [4mgroup[24m, [1mcreate[0m [4mowner[24m [4mgroup[24m[m
              Immediately  after rotation (before the [1mpostrotate[0m script is run) the log file is[m
              created (with the same name as the log file just rotated).   [4mmode[24m  specifies  the[m
              mode  for  the log file in octal (the same as [1mchmod[0m(2)), [4mowner[24m specifies the user[m
              name who will own the log file, and [4mgroup[24m specifies the group the log  file  will[m
              belong  to.  Any  of  the log file attributes may be omitted, in which case those[m
              attributes for the new file will use the same values as the original log file for[m
              the omitted attributes. This option can be disabled using the [1mnocreate[0m option.[m
[m
       [1mcreateolddir[0m [4mmode[24m [4mowner[24m [4mgroup[24m[m
              If  the  directory  specified  by [1molddir[0m directive does not exist, it is created.[m
              [4mmode[24m specifies the mode for the [1molddir[0m directory in octal (the same as [1mchmod[0m(2)),[m
              [4mowner[24m specifies the user name who will own the [1molddir[0m directory, and [4mgroup[24m speciâ€[m
              fies the group the [1molddir[0m directory will belong to. This option can  be  disabled[m
              using the [1mnocreateolddir[0m option.[m
[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 182 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1mdaily[0m  Log files are rotated every day.[m
[m
       [1mdateext[0m[m
              Archive  old  versions of log files adding a date extension like YYYYMMDD instead[m
              of simply adding a number. The extension may be configured using  the  [1mdateformat[0m[m
              and [1mdateyesterday[0m options.[m
[m
       [1mdateformat[0m [4mformat_string[24m[m
              Specify the extension for [1mdateext[0m using the notation similar to [1mstrftime[0m(3) funcâ€[m
              tion. Only %Y %m %d %H and %s specifiers  are  allowed.   The  default  value  is[m
              -%Y%m%d except hourly, which uses -%Y%m%d%H as default value.  Note that also the[m
              character separating log name from  the  extension  is  part  of  the  dateformat[m
              string.  The system clock must be set past Sep 9th 2001 for %s to work correctly.[m
              Note that the datestamps generated by this  format  must  be  lexically  sortable[m
              (i.e.,  first  the year, then the month then the day. e.g., 2001/12/01 is ok, but[m
              01/12/2001 is not, since 01/11/2002 would sort lower while it is later).  This is[m
              because  when  using  the [1mrotate[0m option, logrotate sorts all rotated filenames to[m
              find out which logfiles are older and should be removed.[m
[m
       [1mdateyesterday[0m[m
              Use yesterday's instead of today's date to create the [1mdateext[0m extension, so  that[m
              the  rotated  log  file has a date in its name that is the same as the timestamps[m
              within it.[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 209 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       [1mdelaycompress[0m[m
              Postpone compression of the previous log file to the next rotation  cycle.   This[m
              only has effect when used in combination with [1mcompress[0m.  It can be used when some[m
              program cannot be told to close its logfile and thus might  continue  writing  to[m
              the previous log file for some time.[m
[m
       [1mextension[0m [4mext[24m[m
              Log  files with [4mext[24m extension can keep it after the rotation.  If compression  is[m
              used,  the compression extension (normally [1m.gz[0m) appears after  [4mext[24m.  For  example[m
              you  have  a  logfile  named  mylog.foo  and  want to rotate it to mylog.1.foo.gz[m
              instead of mylog.foo.1.gz.[m
[m
       [1mhourly[0m Log files are rotated every hour. Note that usually [4mlogrotate[24m is configured to be[m
              run by cron daily. You have to change this configuration and run [4mlogrotate[24m hourly[m
              to be able to really rotate logs hourly.[m
[m
       [1mifempty[0m[m
              Rotate the log file even  if  it  is  empty,  overriding  the  [1mnotifempty[0m  option[m
              ([1mifempty[0m is the default).[m
[m
       [1minclude[0m [4mfile_or_directory[24m[m
              Reads  the  file  given  as  an  argument  as if it was included inline where the[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 235 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              [1minclude[0m directive appears. If a directory is given, most of  the  files  in  that[m
              directory  are  read  in alphabetic order before processing of the including file[m
              continues. The only files which are ignored are files which are not regular files[m
              (such  as  directories and named pipes) and files whose names end with one of the[m
              taboo extensions, as specified by the [1mtabooext[0m directive.[m
[m
       [1mmail[0m [4maddress[24m[m
              When a log is rotated out-of-existence, it is  mailed  to  [4maddress[24m.  If  no  mail[m
              should be generated by a particular log, the [1mnomail[0m directive may be used.[m
[m
       [1mmailfirst[0m[m
              When using the [1mmail[0m command, mail the just-rotated file, instead of the about-to-[m
              expire file.[m
[m
       [1mmaillast[0m[m
              When using the [1mmail[0m command, mail the about-to-expire file, instead of the  just-[m
              rotated file (this is the default).[m
[m
       [1mmaxage[0m [4mcount[24m[m
              Remove  rotated logs older than <count> days. The age is only checked if the logâ€[m
              file is to be rotated. The files are mailed to the configured address if [1mmaillast[0m[m
              and [1mmail[0m are configured.[m
[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 263 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1mmaxsize[0m [4msize[24m[m
              Log files are rotated when they grow bigger than [4msize[24m bytes even before the addiâ€[m
              tionally specified time  interval  ([1mdaily[0m,  [1mweekly[0m,  [1mmonthly[0m,  or  [1myearly[0m).   The[m
              related [1msize[0m option is similar except that it is mutually exclusive with the time[m
              interval options, and it causes log files to be rotated without  regard  for  the[m
              last  rotation  time.  When [1mmaxsize[0m is used, both the size and timestamp of a log[m
              file are considered.[m
[m
       [1mminsize[0m  [4msize[24m[m
              Log files are rotated when they grow bigger than [4msize[24m bytes, but not  before  the[m
              additionally  specified  time  interval ([1mdaily[0m, [1mweekly[0m, [1mmonthly[0m, or [1myearly[0m).  The[m
              related [1msize[0m option is similar except that it is mutually exclusive with the time[m
              interval  options,  and  it causes log files to be rotated without regard for the[m
              last rotation time.  When [1mminsize[0m is used, both the size and timestamp of  a  log[m
              file are considered.[m
[m
       [1mmissingok[0m[m
              If  the  log file is missing, go on to the next one without issuing an error mesâ€[m
              sage. See also [1mnomissingok[0m.[m
[m
       [1mmonthly[0m[m
              Log files are rotated the first time [1mlogrotate[0m is run in a month  (this  is  norâ€[m
              mally on the first day of the month).[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 291 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       [1mnocompress[0m[m
              Old versions of log files are not compressed. See also [1mcompress[0m.[m
[m
       [1mnocopy[0m Do  not  copy  the  original log file and leave it in place.  (this overrides the[m
              [1mcopy[0m option).[m
[m
       [1mnocopytruncate[0m[m
              Do not truncate the original log file in place after creating a copy (this  overâ€[m
              rides the [1mcopytruncate[0m option).[m
[m
       [1mnocreate[0m[m
              New log files are not created (this overrides the [1mcreate[0m option).[m
[m
       [1mnocreateolddir[0m[m
              [1molddir[0m directory is not created by logrotate when it does not exist.[m
[m
       [1mnodelaycompress[0m[m
              Do  not  postpone compression of the previous log file to the next rotation cycle[m
              (this overrides the [1mdelaycompress[0m option).[m
[m
       [1mnodateext[0m[m
              Do not archive  old versions of log files with date extension (this overrides the[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 317 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              [1mdateext[0m option).[m
[m
       [1mnomail[0m Don't mail old log files to any address.[m
[m
       [1mnomissingok[0m[m
              If a log file does not exist, issue an error. This is the default.[m
[m
       [1mnoolddir[0m[m
              Logs  are  rotated  in the same directory the log normally resides in (this overâ€[m
              rides the [1molddir[0m option).[m
[m
       [1mnosharedscripts[0m[m
              Run [1mprerotate[0m and [1mpostrotate[0m scripts for every log file which is rotated (this is[m
              the  default,  and  overrides the [1msharedscripts[0m option). The absolute path to the[m
              log file is passed as first argument to the script.  If  the  scripts  exit  with[m
              error, the remaining actions will not be executed for the affected log only.[m
[m
       [1mnoshred[0m[m
              Do not use [1mshred[0m when deleting old log files. See also [1mshred[0m.[m
[m
       [1mnotifempty[0m[m
              Do not rotate the log if it is empty (this overrides the [1mifempty[0m option).[m
[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 347 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1molddir[0m [4mdirectory[24m[m
              Logs  are  moved  into  [4mdirectory[24m for rotation. The [4mdirectory[24m must be on the same[m
              physical device as the log file  being  rotated,  unless  [1mcopy[0m,  [1mcopytruncate[0m  or[m
              [1mrenamecopy[0m  option is used. The [4mdirectory[24m is assumed to be relative to the direcâ€[m
              tory holding the log file unless an absolute path name is  specified.  When  this[m
              option  is used all old versions of the log end up in [4mdirectory[24m.  This option may[m
              be overridden by the [1mnoolddir[0m option.[m
[m
       [1mpostrotate[0m/[1mendscript[0m[m
              The lines between [1mpostrotate[0m and [1mendscript[0m (both of which must appear on lines by[m
              themselves)  are  executed  (using  [1m/bin/sh[0m) after the log file is rotated. These[m
              directives may only appear inside a log file definition. Normally,  the  absolute[m
              path  to the log file is passed as first argument to the script. If [1msharedscripts[0m[m
              is specified, whole pattern is passed to the script.   See  also  [1mprerotate[0m.  See[m
              [1msharedscripts[0m and [1mnosharedscripts[0m for error handling.[m
[m
       [1mprerotate[0m/[1mendscript[0m[m
              The  lines between [1mprerotate[0m and [1mendscript[0m (both of which must appear on lines by[m
              themselves) are executed (using [1m/bin/sh[0m) before the log file is rotated and  only[m
              if  the  log  will actually be rotated. These directives may only appear inside a[m
              log file definition. Normally, the absolute path to the log  file  is  passed  as[m
              first  argument  to the script.  If  [1msharedscripts[0m is specified, whole pattern is[m
              passed to the script.  See also  [1mpostrotate[0m.   See  [1msharedscripts[0m  and  [1mnosharedâ€[0m[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 377 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              [1mscripts[0m for error handling.[m
[m
       [1mfirstaction[0m/[1mendscript[0m[m
              The  lines  between [1mfirstaction[0m and [1mendscript[0m (both of which must appear on lines[m
              by themselves) are executed (using [1m/bin/sh[0m) once before all log files that  match[m
              the wildcarded pattern are rotated, before prerotate script is run and only if at[m
              least one log will actually be rotated.  These directives may only appear  inside[m
              a  log  file definition. Whole pattern is passed to the script as first argument.[m
              If the script exits with error, no further processing is done. See  also  [1mlastacâ€[0m[m
              [1mtion[0m.[m
[m
       [1mlastaction[0m/[1mendscript[0m[m
              The lines between [1mlastaction[0m and [1mendscript[0m (both of which must appear on lines by[m
              themselves) are executed (using [1m/bin/sh[0m) once after all log files that match  the[m
              wildcarded  pattern  are  rotated,  after postrotate script is run and only if at[m
              least one log is rotated. These directives may only appear inside a log file defâ€[m
              inition.  Whole  pattern is passed to the script as first argument. If the script[m
              exits with error, just an error message is shown (as this is  the  last  action).[m
              See also [1mfirstaction[0m.[m
[m
       [1mpreremove[0m/[1mendscript[0m[m
              The  lines between [1mpreremove[0m and [1mendscript[0m (both of which must appear on lines by[m
              themselves) are executed (using [1m/bin/sh[0m) once just before removal of a log  file.[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 402 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              The  logrotate  will  pass the name of file which is soon to be removed. See also[m
              [1mfirstaction[0m.[m
[m
       [1mrotate[0m [4mcount[24m[m
              Log files are rotated [4mcount[24m times before being removed or mailed to  the  address[m
              specified  in  a  [1mmail[0m  directive. If [4mcount[24m is 0, old versions are removed rather[m
              than rotated.[m
[m
       [1msize[0m [4msize[24m[m
              Log files are rotated only if they grow bigger then [4msize[24m bytes. If [4msize[24m  is  folâ€[m
              lowed  by  [4mk[24m, the size is assumed to be in kilobytes.  If the [4mM[24m is used, the size[m
              is in megabytes, and if [4mG[24m is used, the size is in gigabytes. So  [4msize[24m  [4m100[24m,  [4msize[24m[m
              [4m100k[24m, [4msize[24m [4m100M[24m and [4msize[24m [4m100G[24m are all valid.[m
[m
       [1msharedscripts[0m[m
              Normally,  [1mprerotate[0m and [1mpostrotate[0m scripts are run for each log which is rotated[m
              and the absolute path to the log file is passed as first argument to the  script.[m
              That  means  a single script may be run multiple times for log file entries which[m
              match multiple files (such as the [4m/var/log/news/*[24m example). If  [1msharedscripts[0m  is[m
              specified, the scripts are only run once, no matter how many logs match the wildâ€[m
              carded pattern, and whole pattern is passed to them.  However,  if  none  of  the[m
              logs  in the pattern require rotating, the scripts will not be run at all. If the[m
              scripts exit with error, the remaining actions will not be executed for any logs.[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 428 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              This option overrides the [1mnosharedscripts[0m option and implies [1mcreate[0m option.[m

       [1mshred[0m  Delete  log  files  using  [1mshred[0m -u instead of unlink().  This should ensure that[m
              logs are not readable after their scheduled deletion; this  is  off  by  default.[m
              See also [1mnoshred[0m.[m
[m
       [1mshredcycles[0m [4mcount[24m[m
              Asks  GNU  [1mshred[0m(1)  to overwrite log files [1mcount[0m times before deletion.  Without[m
              this option, [1mshred[0m's default will be used.[m
[m
       [1mstart[0m [4mcount[24m[m
              This is the number to use as the base for rotation. For example, if  you  specify[m
              0,  the  logs  will  be  created with a .0 extension as they are rotated from the[m
              original log files.  If you specify 9, log files will be created with a .9, skipâ€[m
              ping  0-8.   Files  will  still be rotated the number of times specified with the[m
              [1mrotate[0m directive.[m
[m
       [1msu[0m [4muser[24m [4mgroup[24m[m
              Rotate log files  set  under  this  user  and  group  instead  of  using  default[m
              user/group  (usually  root).  [4muser[24m  specifies the user name used for rotation and[m
              [4mgroup[24m specifies the group used for rotation.[m
[m
       [1mtabooext[0m [+] [4mlist[24m[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 454 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K              The current taboo extension list is changed (see the [1minclude[0m directive for inforâ€[m

[m
       [1mweekly[0m Log files are rotated if the current weekday is less than the weekday of the last[m
              rotation or if more than a week has passed since the last rotation. This is  norâ€[m
              mally the same as rotating logs on the first day of the week, but it works better[m
              if [4mlogrotate[24m is not run every night.[m
[m
       [1myearly[0m Log files are rotated if the current year is not the same as the last rotation.[m

[?1049h[?1h=LOGROTATE(8)                                                                      System Administrator's Manual                                                                      LOGROTATE(8)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       logrotate â€ rotates, compresses, and mails system logs[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m [[1m-dv[0m] [[1m-f[0m|[1m--force[0m] [[1m-s[0m|[1m--state[0m [4mfile[24m] [4mconfig_file[24m ..[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mlogrotate[0m is designed to ease administration of systems that generate large numbers of log files.  It allows automatic rotation, compression, removal, and mailing of log files.  Each log[m
       file may be handled daily, weekly, monthly, or when it grows too large.[m
[m
       Normally, [1mlogrotate[0m is run as a daily cron job.  It will not modify a log multiple times in one day unless the criterion for that log is based on the log's size and  [1mlogrotate[0m  is  being[m
       run multiple times each day, or unless the [1m-f[0m or [1m--force[0m option is used.[m
[m
       Any  number  of  config  files  may be given on the command line. Later config files may override the options given in earlier files, so the order in which the [1mlogrotate[0m config files are[m
       listed is important.  Normally, a single config file which includes any other config files which are needed should be used.  See below for more information on  how  to  use  the  [1minclude[0m[m
       directive to accomplish this.  If a directory is given on the command line, every file in that directory is used as a config file.[m
[m
       If no command line arguments are given, [1mlogrotate[0m will print version and copyright information, along with a short usage summary.  If any errors occur while rotating logs, [1mlogrotate[0m will[m
       exit with non-zero status.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
[7m Manual page logrotate(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1m-?[0m, [1m--help[0m[m
              Prints help message.[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--debug[0m[m
              Turns on debug mode and implies [1m-v[0m.  In debug mode, no changes will be made to the logs or to the [1mlogrotate[0m state file.[m
[m
       [1m-f[0m, [1m--force[0m[m
              Tells [1mlogrotate[0m to force the rotation, even if it doesn't think this is necessary.  Sometimes this is useful after adding new entries to a [1mlogrotate[0m config file,  or  if  old  log[m
              files have been removed by hand, as the new files will be created, and logging will continue correctly.[m
[m
       [1m-m[0m, [1m--mail[0m [1m<command>[0m[m
              Tells [1mlogrotate[0m which command to use when mailing logs. This command should accept two arguments: 1) the subject of the message, and 2) the recipient. The command must then read a[m
              message on standard input and mail it to the recipient. The default mail command is [1m/bin/mail[0m [1m-s[0m.[m
[m
       [1m-s[0m, [1m--state[0m [1m<statefile>[0m[m
              Tells [1mlogrotate[0m to use an alternate state file.  This is useful if logrotate is being run as a different  user  for  various  sets  of  log  files.   The  default  state  file  is[m
              [4m/var/lib/logrotate/logrotate.status[24m.[m
[m
       [1m--usage[0m[m
              Prints a short usage message.[m
[m
       +[1m-v[0m, [1m--verbose[0m[m
              Turns on verbose mode.[m

       Please  use  wildcards  with  caution.   If you specify *, [1mlogrotate[0m will rotate all files, including previously rotated ones.  A way around this is to use the [1molddir[0m directive or a more[m
       exact wildcard (such as *.log).[m

       Here is more information on the directives which may be included in a [1mlogrotate[0m configuration file:[m
[m
       [1mcompress[0m[m
              Old versions of log files are compressed with [1mgzip[0m(1) by default. See also [1mnocompress[0m.[m
[m
       [1mcompresscmd[0m[m
              Specifies which command to use to compress log files.  The default is [1mgzip[0m.  See also [1mcompress[0m.[m
[m
       [1muncompresscmd[0m[m
              Specifies which command to use to uncompress log files.  The default is [1mgunzip[0m.[m
[m
       [1mcompressext[0m[m
              Specifies which extension to use on compressed logfiles, if compression is enabled.  The default follows that of the configured compression command.[m
[m
       [1mcompressoptions[0m[m
              Command line options may be passed to the compression program, if one is in use.  The default, for [1mgzip[0m(1), is "-6" (biased towards high compression at the expense of speed).   If[m
              you use a different compression command, you may need to change the [1mcompressoptions[0m to match.[m
